Traditional Chinese Medicine Groups Oppose Fee Collection on Prescriptions 170

Jointly Petitioned the Municipal Party Headquarters to Stop It Yesterday

Legitimacy of Traditional Chinese Medicine Depends Entirely on Payment

Violates the Declaration Exempting Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies

The Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Association, the Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, and the All-China Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, along with all executive supervisors, filed a petition to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters regarding the Shanghai branch of the National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall collecting fees per prescription, requesting that they immediately stop it nearby, and forward it to the Central Party Headquarters to consult the Executive Yuan to order the Hall to cancel it. The petition concerned the Shanghai branch of the Central National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall illegally levying fees per prescription from Traditional Chinese Medicine practitioners. It requested investigation and approval, earnestly requesting immediate stoppage nearby, and forwarding it to the Central Party Headquarters to consult the Executive Yuan to order the Hall to cancel it. The association stated that it received a letter from the Shanghai branch of the National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall on March 25 of this year, stating that all prescriptions used by Traditional Chinese Medicine practitioners practicing in the city should be submitted to the Traditional Chinese Medicine branch for stamping and pay a branch fee of one dollar, and that the payment rules for medical prescriptions were distributed to the association. After the announcement, the association's members believed that the branch's collection of fees per prescription was a form of taxation, which had no legal basis, was excessively detailed, and was difficult to implement. After conveying this to the branch, the branch director Lu Zhong'an disregarded public opinion and insisted on his own way. The Central National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall is an organization to assist in the development of Chinese medicine, and is absolutely a medical and health organization. The significance is stated in the first article of the organizational charter of the Central National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall. The branches in various provinces and cities are subordinate institutions, and their nature should not be different. The acquisition of its funds should first request the local government to allocate subsidies, and if it is insufficient, then the branch board of directors may raise funds. The collection of these funds is the duty of the branch board of directors, not the right of the Traditional Chinese Medicine branch. Therefore, it can only be persuaded by the board of directors to help with expenses. To levy it in the name of the branch and enforce it by force is illegal. Its own organization is only responsible for organizing academics and does not have any administrative power. The regulations are clear and do not allow distortion. Branch director Lu Zhong'an has neither applied to the local government for subsidies in accordance with the law (according to the original letter from the branch) nor announced a budget. How can he know in advance that the subsidy will be insufficient in the future, and levy taxes without fear of distorting the law and openly suppressing it? According to the regulations on the exercise of governance promulgated by the National Government on July 10, 1929, even if the branch is indeed an administrative agency, it may not independently formulate and implement it. According to Article 6 of the branch's payment rules for medical prescriptions, pharmacies will recognize physicians that have the branch's seal as legitimate Chinese medicine physicians, and dispense medicine according to the prescription. Otherwise, it will be considered a violation of the rules. That is, Traditional Chinese Medicine practitioners who are recognized as legitimate and licensed by the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau can be given the name of illegitimate Chinese medicine practitioners simply by not paying one cent of expenses. Furthermore, according to Article 9 of the rules, prescriptions written by patients themselves without the name and seal of a physician are not subject to this restriction, which is tantamount to organizing the agency of Traditional Chinese Medicine and assisting in the popularization of divining prescriptions and immortal prescriptions, secretly cultivating superstitious psychology among the people. All of this not only disrupts the administrative system, but also openly violates the declaration of the National Government in 1928 exempting miscellaneous taxes and levies, as well as the intention of the Ministry to eliminate injustice and protect the lives of the people. It is extremely illegal and beyond authority. The Central National Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall did not examine the situation and correct it. I hope that the Ministry will be concerned about the people's grievances and see far and wide. In addition to filing a complaint with the Executive Yuan in accordance with the law, we should jointly file a petition for investigation and approval, and earnestly request that the illegal original order be immediately stopped nearby, and forwarded to the Central Party Headquarters, and consult the Executive Yuan, to order the Hall to cancel the illegal original order, which would be a great kindness.

Third Time Planning to Play Chinese Music

Record of Robbery Encountered by Brothers, Customers of a Fur Shop 172

Unforeseen Disaster, Brother Dies, Brother Injured

Yuchenghe Fur Shop, No. 112 Jixiang Lane, Jixiang Street, French Concession, has been in business for more than 30 years and has developed quite well. At around 7 p.m. last night, just after the shop had finished dinner, two customers from Zhenjiang, Tang Jingen (36 years old) and Tang Jinbiao (27 years old), brothers, suddenly arrived to inquire whether a batch of goods shipped from Tianjin had arrived in Shanghai. However, just as the Tang brothers sat down and the tea boy was serving tea, three robbers broke in from outside the door. One was wearing a white-gray robe and two were wearing black gowns. All were around 30 years old. One of the robbers, speaking imperfect Shanghai dialect, first asked if the surname was Wen and if they had come here. At that time, Tang Jingen felt that the three men were flustered and their actions were erratic, and remembered that they were definitely not good people. He wanted to get up and close the door. Seeing that the situation was not good, the three robbers turned around and ran out, trying to escape. The Tang brothers followed and chased them out, shouting for the capture of robbers. When they chased to the entrance of Jixiang Lane, No. 120, in front of the Mori Yuen Hing glass shop, one of the robbers turned around and fired three shots at the Tang brothers. Jingen was shot in the chest and fell to the ground. Jinbiao was shot in the right arm. When nearby detectives heard the alarm and rushed to the scene, the three robbers had already disappeared. The detectives were dispatched by the police station to send the Tang brothers to Renji Hospital. Jingen died in the hospital at 8:10 p.m. due to serious injuries. Jinbiao was not seriously injured. The hospital notified the police station, which in turn instructed the Tongren Fuyuan branch to send undertakers to carry Jingen's body to the autopsy room, and report to the Second Special District Court tomorrow for a gun examination.

Coincidentally, a Chinese Policeman = British Soldier, Comrades Kill Each Other

Both Use Poisonous Hands Due to Grievances and Revenge

Chinese and British Killers Both Commit Suicide in Fear of Punishment

Chinese Policeman Shoots and Kills Police Chief 173

Song Huchen, from Feicheng County, Shandong Province, was 38 years old and lived on Haifang Road, Gordon Road, West Shanghai. He was the Chinese policeman No. 322 in the third patrol of the Disraeli Road police station in the Public Concession. At around 11 a.m. yesterday, as it was the time for the Chinese policemen to change shifts, Song led more than a dozen Chinese policemen to the team from the police station. When they approached No. 1408 Disraeli Road near North Sichuan Road, a Chinese policeman No. 1889 in the team suddenly shouted, "Slow down, Song!" When Song looked back and was about to question him, the Chinese policeman No. 1889 had already pulled out the pistol provided by his superior, secretly loaded a bullet, and fired four shots at Song, all hitting vital points. Song still hoped to escape and ran forward with all his strength, to the entrance of Changxing Laundry, No. 1410, at the intersection of Disraeli Road and North Sichuan Road, and finally fell to the ground due to exhaustion. Seeing this, the other Chinese policemen in the team quickly surrounded the Chinese policeman who had committed the crime. In desperation, the policeman turned his hand and fired a shot at his own head, and fell to the ground. Seeing that the disaster was expanding, the policemen quickly returned to the police station to report, and sent the injured police chief and the Chinese policeman who committed the crime to the Municipal Council Hospital on Ward Road for treatment. However, both died of their injuries on the way. The two bodies were then sent to the Phalen Road autopsy room to be reported to the court for examination. After investigation, reporters learned that the cause of this disaster was actually due to the fact that at around 7 p.m. on the 24th, when Song was patrolling near Disraeli Road, he saw that the policeman No. 1889 was not on duty. After inquiring, he learned that the policeman had entrusted his attendance diary to a nearby police officer, and then went to gamble nearby. Song found him at the gambling place and reported it to the police chief. After discussion by the superiors, the policeman was demoted. The announcement was posted at 10 a.m. yesterday morning. When the policeman No. 1889 saw it, he harbored resentment and plotted revenge, but he did not expect that he would take such a poisonous hand. Song's family only left behind a wife and a daughter, and his death was very sad. The Chinese policeman No. 1889 who committed the crime was named Li Chunhe, from Tianjin. At the same time, the police station was very saddened by the fact that policeman Song was killed due to a public grievance, and was planning for the aftermath.

British Soldier Shoots and Wounds Officer 174

According to the North China Daily News, a British duty soldier, Glover, shot and wounded an officer in the YMCA shack near the Jiaozhou Road barracks yesterday morning and threatened the soldiers of the regiment, preventing them from approaching. When detectives tricked him into being arrested, he shot himself and died in the British Military Hospital on Central Road. The British police court sent someone to examine the body yesterday afternoon and scheduled a trial for Saturday. When the case occurred, the vicinity of the Jiaozhou Road barracks was greatly shaken, and the British community regarded it as an unusual event. Several people tried to persuade him to release the gun and surrender, but Glover did not listen. The details of the case suggest that there may have been unexpected grievances. It is believed that the truth will come out after the trial. According to the report, Glover was a young soldier, only 26 years old, who had only been in Shanghai for over a year. He is currently assigned to the Second Battalion of the East Lancashire Regiment of the British Army. He was assigned to the British Miqin team to escort cars, so he received a pistol and six bullets every day when he went from the Jiaozhou Road barracks to the car parking lot. As usual, he went to the duty team barracks with a gun to serve on a car yesterday morning. At 10 a.m., the car went out, but Gray could not be found. He called the military lawyer of the Jiaozhou Road barracks, Pinard, and began searching. It is said that Glover had been summoned to Pinard's office for reprimand for violating the rules, but it seemed that there was no hard feeling afterward. Later, when Pinard found the YMCA shack, Glover saw him approaching and knew that the purpose was himself. He immediately opened fire, wounding Pinard's right hand. Pinard then withdrew and called other soldiers to assist. The staff of the YMCA also went to persuade him, but all were ineffective. A few minutes later, Glover saw that the British soldiers had surrounded the outside of the shack and fired two more shots. As Glover had no way to escape and the other soldiers did not want to be targets, they had no intention of entering to arrest him, and a stalemate was formed. Later, the authorities decided to ask the patrol to assist and called the Gordon Road police station. At around 11 a.m., a Western detective in a bulletproof vest rushed to the scene, walked into the shack, and persuaded Glover to release the gun and surrender. He was about to achieve his goal when Glover suddenly aimed the muzzle at his forehead and pulled the trigger, committing suicide. However, he did not die at the time. It was not until 12:30 p.m. that he was sent to the British Military Hospital on Central Road, and he died at 1:10 p.m.

Friend Inside, Husband Blocked Outside 175

Liu Suqin's Romance Is Evident

Wife Elopes at Night, Husband Sues Mother-in-Law

Fu Shiyan, from Anhui, was serving in the military. His wife, Liu Suqin, is the daughter of Liu Wangshi from Jiangbei, currently 31 years old. She has been married to Fu for eight years and has three children, both sons and daughters. They originally lived in Dingfeng Lane, Fujian Road. Last winter, because Fu's friend was working in Hunan Province, Fu also went to Hunan on October 16th to seek employment. He frequently entrusted household affairs to his mother-in-law, Liu Wangshi, for care. Shortly after, his venture failed, and he returned to Shanghai on November 19th of the lunar calendar. Unexpectedly, upon arriving home, his wife and children were nowhere to be found. He inquired of the neighbors and learned that after he left, his wife, instigated by her mother, had completely changed her behavior. She had mingled with prostitutes, turning the home into a brothel and using the residence as a temporary meeting place, which led to the landlord's disapproval and eviction. Therefore, she had moved to the remaining rooms of Dasheng Hospital near Sanma Road and Yunnan Road. Fu immediately rushed there to find her. According to a Dr. Yi at the hospital, although there had been tenants recently, none were named Fu, but they had heard the surname Zhang. At this moment, a maid came downstairs. Fu recognized her as the one he had hired before he left. Believing that a breakthrough was possible, he decided to ascend the stairs, hoping to have a heartfelt conversation with his wife, whom he was apart from. Unexpectedly, the maid physically blocked him, preventing him from entering the room. At that time, Liu Suqin also emerged from the room, looking drowsy with her robe half-undone. Seeing this, Fu suspected she had just woken up from a daytime nap. He questioned her about the reason for preventing him from entering. The woman said that a friend was inside and it was inconvenient for him to see. Fu listened to her words and observed the movements inside the room. In an instant, he suddenly saw a man wearing an overcoat escape from the window. By the time Fu rushed into the room, he was long gone. Fu then severely scolded his wife, and the sounds of his reproaches did not cease until midnight. That very night, Liu Suqin abandoned her children, left the house alone, and disappeared without a trace. Fu, believing that his wife's departure was due to his mother-in-law's instigation, filed a criminal complaint of interference with marriage against Liu Wangshi. The First Special District Court has already issued a summons for a hearing. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui continued the trial. After the plaintiff, Fu Shiyan, described the circumstances of the case, he also stated that the defendant escaped that night while he was out bathing and that all his valuables and clothes were taken away. He also stated that his marriage with Liu Suqin had been arranged through a matchmaker and that a marriage certificate existed. Dr. Yi was also brought to court to testify about Liu Suqin renting the room from him, saying that he did not know her background since she only lived there for five days. When questioned, the defendant, Liu Wangshi, claimed ignorance of the charges, saying that her daughter had eloped with Fu. She added that now that a formal son-in-law had taken her daughter away, it had nothing to do with her, and that her daughter was already in court. Liu Suqin also confessed to eloping and denied being a prostitute while Fu was away, as well as denying any theft this time. The judge, deeming further investigation necessary, adjourned the hearing.

North China Daily News Director Davis' Midnight Adventure 176

Friend Wightman Threatens with a Gun

Davis' Quick Thinking Saves the Day

English Police Court Hearing Yesterday 177

The Ta Mei Wan Pao reports that Englishman Wightman, accused of breaking into the home of Davis, Managing Director of the North China Daily News, and threatening him with a gun, was heard again in the English Police Court this morning (26th). Lawyer Livingstone, who had represented Davis and the police on Monday, stated that he was unable to continue due to other matters and was replaced by Mustard. Mustard then read the original charge, adding two more counts: one for assaulting Davis and one for intending to injure Davis with a gun. Mustard elaborated on the case, saying that the defendant and Davis had known each other for many years and had a good relationship. Before Christmas last year, the defendant visited, and after Davis came out to see him, the defendant behaved rudely, showing a section of the North China Daily News commentary from December 16th, pointing out hidden satire and insinuations against the defendant, and making threatening remarks, demanding satisfaction. In fact, the defendant's accusations were completely imaginary and unfounded. Davis explained this, and the defendant seemed quite satisfied and left. Not long after, the defendant visited again, asking for help in finding a job. Davis told him he would keep an eye out. The defendant left happily again. Then, the day before the incident, which was the 21st of this month at 8 a.m., the defendant visited Davis again. Previously, the defendant had visited Davis three times, but he was not in. This morning, when he saw Davis, he spoke quite aggressively, took out a document, and asked Davis to sign it. Davis read it over once but did not understand it very well and refused to sign. According to what Davis had learned, the defendant was suffering from a mental illness at the time. Although there was a slight dispute, Davis still comforted him and told him to leave. At 8:30 p.m. that evening, he came again, but Davis told him that he had a banquet to attend and left. The next morning at 5:45 a.m., Davis was awakened by the sound of footsteps and saw the defendant approaching his bed, followed by a servant. The defendant took out another document and threatened loudly, saying that if Davis did not sign it, he would blow up the whole house. He also took out a revolver and pointed it at Davis' head, only inches away, threatening to shoot if he did not sign. Davis, just awakened from his dream, took the paper and glanced at it. He picked up a pencil from the table beside the bed and pretended to sign, hoping to take the opportunity to seize the gun. Then he said that he should sign with a fountain pen and asked the defendant if he had one. The defendant was about to untie the buttons of his raincoat to take out the pen, but because he was in a hurry, he could not untie the buttons and placed the gun on the table. As he took the pen from his pocket, Davis cleverly stretched out a foot and knocked a long gown from the end of the bed to the floor. Then, while the defendant was looking down, he quickly grabbed the gun from the table and hid it under the blanket. The defendant looked back and saw that the gun was gone, and he shouted loudly, saying that Davis had hidden his gun. Davis pretended that the servant had taken it. The two argued for a long time. Davis then quietly put the gun in his sleeve, got out of bed, and went downstairs before the defendant. The defendant followed, punching and kicking Davis no less than five or six times. When they reached the bottom of the stairs, Davis pretended to ask the servants, "Who took this gun?" After a long time, as the gun could not be found, the defendant cursed and left. After that, Davis reported to the police and had the defendant arrested. Inside the defendant's gun were five bullets, one of which was already in the chamber, and the safety was not on. Davis secretly put the safety on and then handed it over to the police.

The Fresh Pork Industry Responds to the Social Bureau with Proposed Measures to Crack Down on Inferior Coins 180

The Use of Auxiliary Currency Should Be Limited by Law

The Fresh Pork Industry Association of this city, due to the prevalence of inferior coins in the market, in meat transactions, often calculates silver coins into silver dollars, but when converting them, a heavy discount is required, resulting in significant losses in a single transaction. They have submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department, the Social Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the government for a crackdown. Subsequently, Chairman Zhang Jitang of the association was summoned by the Social Bureau and consulted on effective measures to crack down. He then continued to present measures, stating in the original report: "Submitting this report for continued submission of measures to crack down on inferior coins, hoping for your review. The association previously received a report from member Chunyuan Xing, stating that inferior coins are rampant in the market, resulting in significant losses in a single transaction for merchants. They have submitted a request to your bureau, requesting strict orders to crack down, and requesting the government to uniformly mint, recover, and recoin, and at the same time, send a letter to the customs to strictly investigate smuggling and prevent it from spreading. However, the proposal for unified minting involves cumbersome procedures and is likely to be slow to provide relief, and the ban on imports has been requested by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in a telegram to the Ministry of Finance. This ban has been in effect to this day and has not changed. This means that even with meticulous measures, omissions are inevitable, and the effectiveness is not certain. The association has been thinking about this repeatedly and believes that the only way is to set a limit on the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used. The types of currency are divided into main currency and auxiliary currency. The main currency is also called the standard currency. In transactions, no matter how large the amount, the receiver cannot refuse it, hence the name 'unlimited legal tender.' Auxiliary currency is used to assist in the circulation of the main currency, in order to facilitate small payments. It was originally intended to alleviate the scarcity of the main currency and cannot be considered an essential means of payment, so its use can be limited by law. Beyond this limit, the receiver can refuse it, and the creditor must refuse it, hence the name 'limited legal tender.' In countries around the world, such as England, the United States, Germany, and Japan, the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used is regulated by law, with a certain limit. For example, the use of British silver coins cannot exceed two gold pounds, in the United States it cannot exceed ten dollars, the use of German silver coins is limited to within twenty marks, and the limit for the use of Japanese silver coins is ten yen. Because the composition of auxiliary currency is low and the nominal price is greater than the actual price, if it is allowed to be used without limit, people will compete to use auxiliary currency to exchange for goods, and prices may fall as a result. Those who receive large amounts of payment not only face various inconveniences in calculation and transportation but also suffer unexpected losses, such as the heavy discount in this industry. All of this adds up over the year, and the amount is not small. Therefore, a legal limit is set on the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used in order to avoid disturbing the market. The prevalence of inferior coins in Shanghai is due to the uneven market price of silver coins and the profits that traffickers can make, but the lack of restrictions on acceptance is also a major reason. Because there is no limit on the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used, the sales of inferior coins are wider, and the profits are greater. The greater the profits, the more traffickers there are, and this is a reciprocal relationship, resulting in the proliferation of inferior coins in the market. If the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used can be limited by law, setting an appropriate limit as a standard, so that the receiver can refuse payments that exceed this limit, then there will not be many silver coins paid, and there will be no way for inferior coins to mix in. Traffickers will also give up on inferior coins because there is no profit to be made, and the number of inferior coins will decrease day by day without being explicitly banned. Therefore, limiting the amount of auxiliary currency that can be used is an effective way to crack down on inferior coins. Whether this is appropriate is respectfully submitted to your bureau for review, as it is for the public good."

Dock Thugs Forcibly Collect Insurance Fees 184

Claims to be Named Li Yichang

Flees When the Police Arrive

The thugs on the docks along the South City Bund not only extort money from travelers on various pretexts but also demand insurance fees of two or three yuan per month from various civilian ships and sailing vessels operating on the Bund, under the name of insurance. If any of the boat owners are reluctant to pay, the thugs will find excuses to cause trouble, even gathering a crowd to beat them or sending assassins in secret, so that all boat owners operating on the Bund regard the thugs as tigers and wolves. Even if they are extorted, they dare not resist in the slightest. Therefore, the thugs are becoming increasingly reckless. Yesterday afternoon at around 1 p.m., a boat owner named Zhou Afu happened to arrive in Shanghai from Chuansha with passengers and cargo. After arriving at the port, he docked at the Shengyi Wharf on the South City Bund. Suddenly, one of the above-mentioned dock thugs, claiming to be named Li Yichang, came to collect the insurance fee of one yuan and five jiao for this month. Zhou replied that he had no money to pay. Li, upon hearing this, became very angry and immediately grabbed Zhou, punching him. Zhou, unwilling to accept this, handed him over to Liu Fang, the guard of the 16th Gang in that area, and brought him to the 1st Precinct, 1st Station, where Chief Yi conducted a preliminary hearing. Considering Li's misconduct and assuming his ignorance, he was leniently detained for ten days as a warning. Unexpectedly, after Zhou left the station and was about to return to his boat, he saw Li's father, Li Changyong, and his younger brother, Xiao Ningbo, and a dozen others pre-ambushed on the roadside. Upon seeing Zhou, they rushed forward and took out axes and other weapons, intending to harm him and vent Li's anger. Zhou was shocked by the sight and quickly turned around and fled, narrowly escaping. He immediately reported the situation to Chief Yi of the station, who immediately sent patrols to arrest them. However, the thugs had already fled without a trace. He then ordered a formal document to be prepared and sent to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for a thorough investigation.

Interrogation of Kidnappers from Xiaoshan 185

Kidnapper Shen Yun, from Shaoxing, colluded with accomplices in the first month of this year's lunar calendar and went to Tangshan Bay in his hometown of Xiaoshan County to kidnap Chen Zhurong, the 14-year-old only son of the wealthy Chen Tianyou. They brought him to Shanghai and hid him in the home of Chen Shiying, a fellow villager, at 3 Ping'an Fang, Xuehuali Road, in the French Concession. They sent a letter to the victim, demanding a large sum of money for his release. On March 10th, they opened a room at the Huhai Hotel in Baoyu Lane, and ordered their accomplices to negotiate the ransom with the victim's representative at the entrance of Baoyu Lane on Caishi Street. This was discovered by Inspector Jin Jiulin of the French Police, who rushed there with uniformed detectives and arrested Shen and his accomplices Zhang Baichuan, Wang Achang, Lu Ruigao, Zhou Ruifu, Liu Xichen, Chen Shiying, his wife Chen Shengshi, and suspects Gao Bin, Wang Chenshi, Wu Wangshi, and Fu Lanying, totaling twelve men and women. They rescued the hostage and sent them to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. Chen Zhurong, the hostage, was sent by his family to Shanghai to be reunited with them. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. This case has been investigated and concluded by the police. Yesterday, Judge Li Changnian visited Criminal Court One and ordered the defendants to be brought in for further trial (Gao Bin, the seventh defendant, was not brought in because he was being treated in a hospital for illness). First, Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, stated the circumstances of the police solving and investigating the case, saying that it was found that the first defendant, Shen Yun, had acted on the instructions of the fugitive leader Shen Chuangou, colluding with the second, third, fourth, fifth, and sixth defendants to go to Tangshan Bay in Xiaoshan County, Zhejiang Province on February 11th. The next evening, upon arriving at their destination, they broke into the home of the victim, Chen Tianyou, and kidnapped Chen's son to Shanghai, hiding him in the residence of the eighth defendant, Chen Shiying. Afterwards, he received instructions from Shen Chuangou to negotiate with the victim's representative at Room 5 of the Dongchang Hotel on Avenue Joffre on March 4th and received 100 yuan. On March 9th, he went with the third defendant, Wang Achang, to open Room 33 at the Changxing Hotel on Caishi Street, and negotiated with the victim's representative, receiving 200 yuan. After the incident, the defendants were arrested one after another. Now the police are prosecuting the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, and eighth defendants according to Article 1, Clause 1 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits. The remaining defendants are also suspected, and a legal trial is requested. In court, after verifying the words, he ordered the defendants to be interrogated separately. The seven defendants, including Shen, confessed to colluding in kidnapping, concealing, and extorting ransom. The remaining defendants either claimed to have been arrested while visiting friends at the hotel or were arrested with the defendants in the case due to cohabitation. By the time the interrogation was completed, it was past noon. The court ordered a change of date to May 2nd and designated a defender to come to court for further interrogation. The defendants were still sent back for separate detention.

Wen Ying's Mother Sues Diao Ao Ke and Ling Qing Case 188

Involves Feng Mengyun to a Great Extent

Wen Ying's Mother Was Also Countersued in Court

The case of Jianghu fortune teller Diao Ao Ke (also known as Cheng Meixian) and his divorced wife, Cheng Lingqing, along with Feng Mengyun, editor of Da Jing Bao, being sued by Huang Wushi, the mother of the murdered female fortune teller Wen Ying, for offenses such as disruption of the family, was previously tried by the First Special District Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan continued the interrogation. The defendant Ling Qing also surrendered herself and waited to be questioned along with the other two defendants. Judge Wu instructed the plaintiff to state in detail the circumstances of Cheng Lingqing in this case, in addition to what she had already stated in the previous hearing regarding the two defendants Cheng Meixian and Feng Mengyun, which did not need to be repeated. Huang Wushi said that she was accusing Ling Qing of inducing her daughter to engage in prostitution. Her daughter was taken to the Xinhuizhong Hotel and other places by Ling Qing to have her fortune told or to engage in prostitution countless times since she was fourteen years old. Last June, after her daughter told her and after hearing people talk about it after her daughter's death, she went to Xinhuizhong to inquire, and the tea server said that it was indeed true. When questioned, the defendant Ling Qing stated that Wen Ying learned fortune telling at the age of fifteen. At that time, she and Diao Ao Ke were not yet divorced. Diao's fortune telling studio was located in Xinhuizhong, so she often went there with Wen Ying. Later, she felt that the actions of Diao Ao Ke and Wen Ying were irregular. On one hand, she divorced Diao, and on the other hand, she ordered Wen Ying to drop out of school. In total, she was only in her place for a year and a half and did not induce her to engage in prostitution. Huang Wushi, upon hearing her testimony, responded with abusive words. The court then asked the woman about the situation after her daughter was brought to Shanghai from Hangzhou by Cheng et al. However, the woman's answers were not very coherent. She generally said that at first, every time she came to Shanghai to see her daughter, she was accompanied by either Ling Qing or Diao Ao Ke, and the mother and daughter could not talk. She asked Cheng why her daughter was wearing makeup since she was learning photography, and Cheng said that she had to dress like that to take photos with foreigners. Later, her daughter sent a message through someone saying that Diao Ao Ke was very abusive and asked her to find a way to bring her back. When she asked Diao for her daughter, he demanded a certain amount of money for food and lodging. She then asked a battalion commander in Hangzhou to send a letter to Diao Ao Ke, who replied with a photo of Feng Mengyun and her daughter side by side, and said that he would make Feng her son-in-law. The affair between Feng and her daughter happened when she was fifteen years old. Feng Mengyun denied this absolutely and orally stated that he was filing a countersuit against Huang Wushi for defamation, requesting that the woman be placed on bail. Cheng Lingqing also stated that she was filing a countersuit against Huang Wushi. The court then ordered the woman to stand in the defendant's position and asked if she had any defense against the countersuit. Huang Wushi said, "Who is destroying whose reputation? Please investigate clearly." Then, after the lawyers on both sides debated each other, the court stated that the plaintiff still had an ancillary private suit seeking 36,000 yuan in damages from Cheng Meixian and Cheng Lingqing, and ordered the lawyers on both sides to debate this point before announcing that the case would be sentenced on the morning of April 29th. As for Feng Mengyun's request that Huang Wushi be placed on bail, the court stated that it was not necessary.

Suspicion of Wife's Infidelity Leading to Assault with an Axe 189

Bi Jiugao, a Ningbo native residing at a certain address on Dengtuo Road, aged twenty-six, married Wang from the same village last July. After their marriage, their relationship was generally harmonious. However, in January of this year, due to Wang's absence from home for four nights, a quarrel ensued. Wang then returned to her mother's home at 54 Longqing Lane, Dongxi Huade Road. On the fourteenth of that month, Bi went to persuade his wife to return home, but she refused. He then used a razor to wound her neck. After mediation by relatives and friends, Wang was sent back to her husband's house, with promises of reconciliation. However, within a week, another disagreement arose, and Wang left without notice, returning to her mother's house, determined not to return. From then on, the house was empty, and Bi was unable to bring his wife back. Later, through an introduction, he worked as a bathhouse attendant at a hot spring pool on Aiduya Road to earn a living. However, he constantly thought about his wife's infidelity, suspecting she had another lover, which caused him increasing distress. On the evening of the nineteenth of this month, at 11:30 PM, he and two friends secretly went to his mother-in-law's house with a sharp axe to provoke a quarrel with Wang. Wang's sister, Wang A'mei, reported the incident to the Huishan Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. Wang was sent to Shanghai Sanitarium and Hospital for treatment. Judge Xiao Xie-fen presided over the hearing. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the defendant had confessed at the police station to wounding Wang's feet in four places with the axe. The police are prosecuting him for severe injury under Article 294 of the Criminal Code and requested an adjournment. Witness Wang A'mei testified that she is the defendant's sister-in-law. In January, her sister went to her in-laws' house for the New Year's festivities and stayed for several nights. Unexpectedly, the defendant suspected her sister of impropriety and used a razor to wound her neck, leading to a breakdown in their relationship. Fearing his violence, she returned to her mother's house and worked in a cigarette factory to earn a living. On the evening of the nineteenth of this month, the defendant suddenly came to their house with two others to provoke a quarrel. He stopped her mother, and his friend Fu Sheng used an axe to wound her sister in the forehead and feet before fleeing. The defendant claimed that his friend Fu Sheng inflicted the wounds because he was insulted by the wife. He added that they went to intimidate but did not intend to kill Wang. Judge Xiao, after reviewing the evidence, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

Special Article

The Only Way to Remedy the Cotton Mill Industry 201

The crisis in the cotton mill industry did not begin today, nor did the industry's appeals for help. After maintaining a struggle and being forced to reduce labor, the government and society began to pay attention. China is an agricultural country, but cotton production is not abundant. Most Chinese people's clothing is made of cotton textiles. However, domestic cotton cloth has no foothold because it is squeezed by imported goods and domestic and foreign merchant cotton mills. This did not happen overnight. (A) Remote causes: (1) Most Chinese cotton mills are undercapitalized and heavily indebted. (2) Bank interest rates are too high. (3) Factories lack public reserves. (4) Technology is not refined. (5) There is a lack of direct buying and selling of cotton yarn and cloth. (6) Transportation is inconvenient. (B) Recent causes: (1) The Manchurian Incident and the Japanese occupation of Northeast China promoted rural bankruptcy, making farmers' purchasing power weaker. (2) There are many heavy taxes on cotton yarn and cloth. (3) Cotton yarn transportation costs are too high. (4) It has become more difficult to manage workers in recent years. (5) Inland cotton mills are often regarded as fat meat. (6) Gold prices are too high, and imported goods are very expensive. (7) There are too many workers (Japanese factories in China have recently hired many Japanese workers. Each 10,000 spindles only uses 180 to 240 workers, while domestic Chinese factories use 750 workers per 10,000 spindles). (8) There is a worldwide recession, and Japanese cotton goods are being dumped. Most domestic cotton mills suffer from these two causes. The situation is so urgent that if the government only pays lip service to research, investigation, and encouragement, it will be irrelevant. If it really wants to help domestic industries, there is no other way than the following measures. (A) Actively promote and improve cotton planting with a nationally planned and systematic approach. China is short about 3 million piculs of cotton each year, worth more than 130 million silver dollars. Because of the cotton shortage, it has no choice but to buy foreign cotton. Because gold is expensive and silver is cheap, foreign cotton is expensive, and Chinese cotton is also expensive. Cotton yarn depreciates because of slow sales. Expensive cotton and cheap yarn is the biggest crisis in the cotton mill industry. This crisis cannot be fundamentally reversed without actively promoting cotton planting to achieve self-sufficiency. (B) Passively: (1) Eliminate all kinds of heavy taxes on cotton yarn. (2) Revise the unified tax grade and return a few points of the unified tax to Chinese factories as a bonus. (3) Appropriately reduce cotton yarn transportation costs. (4) Reduce loan interest rates. (5) Implement machine consolidation, worker training, cost reduction, and elimination of ineffective employees. If the above items can be implemented one by one, then even in the worst global state, China's cotton mill industry may be able to maintain itself, otherwise it will not only reduce labor by 20% or 30%. In recent years, gold has been expensive and silver has been cheap, and domestic cash has been flowing out. Since the United States abandoned the gold standard, the price of silver has gradually increased, and silver has gradually flowed out. I am afraid that if we do not take preventive measures in the short term, domestic cash will also flow out completely. Then paper money will be rampant, and prices will inevitably soar. Germany's economic situation after the European war will soon be seen in our country. Looking around the country's industry and commerce, everything is in danger. At this time, the government's major policies cannot be changed, otherwise, those who directly suffer are those in industry and commerce, and those who indirectly suffer are the entire Chinese people. The government should actively and vigorously promote the principle of creating production. No matter what kind of industry, as long as it is directly or indirectly beneficial to the whole people, we should do our best to protect it. If there are any destructive or harmful industries that harm the people, we should try our best to eliminate them. Otherwise, even if there is an Adam Smith or someone like him in China today, there will be no way to do well later. I hope that the government officials will start planning quickly.

Spring and Autumn

The Delusional Dream of a Yao King’s Birth

— Zhan Lu

Uncivilized people still cling to the delusional dream of an emperor's birth, hoping that a foundation built on divine mandate will arise from a few kitchen knives and old-fashioned muskets. They loudly chant the fervent slogan of "Uplift the Yao and Destroy the Han," believing that this slogan alone can terrify the souls of the Han people and shatter the courage of the Han race. However, when they come into contact with a regular army, they are like leaves encountering the autumn wind, and amidst cries of suffering, countless lives are lost. Regarding the Yao rebellions in Hanyang, Yining, Xing'an, Quanxian, and other places in Guizhou Province, I know that the wars of the eleventh century, regardless of right or wrong, are fought with material resources. If one's material resources are inferior but one still insists on trying to win, one may achieve occasional victories, but ultimately, failure is inevitable. The Yao people of Guizhou Province serve as a warning.

The reason for the Yao rebellions in Guizhou Province stems from incitement by the Han people. The Yao people, content to live beyond the pale of civilization, have always lived in peace with the Han. Why would they rebel for no reason? It is only because in the past thirty years, as the world has become more civilized, people's hearts have become more cunning. When they encounter the uncarved Yao people, they treat them like smooth operators dealing with country bumpkins, seeking profit through insult and oppression. As a result, the Yao people have forged a deep hatred with the Han people, declaring the birth of a Yao king to rally support. Moreover, Liu Bingwen, a Han man from Xing'an County, has colluded with degenerate Han people, joining the Yao army for opportunistic gains, and their momentum has become quite strong. When the Yao people saw the Han people echoing them, their ambitions grew even stronger, and they immediately raised their flags and launched a rebellion on a large scale, attacking various villages and even capturing county towns in order to realize their plan of "Uplifting the Yao and Destroying the Han." Later, the 19th Division moved its troops to suppress the Yao rebellion, dispatching the 56th and 57th Regiments to take charge of the pacification. It is pitiful to see the Yao people, relying on kitchen knives and shouldering old-fashioned muskets, fall to the ground dead in rows from the bullets! The delusional dream of a Yao king's birth has been shattered by the fierce gunfire, and they have no choice but to succumb to the profound and painful loss!

Cutting wood into weapons and raising poles as flags may have allowed Chen She and Wu Guang to run amok in the uncivilized era of Qin Shi Huang. However, if Qin Shi Huang had possessed a navy, air force, and army, then for every two rebels who cut wood and raised poles, one pair would die. Is there any hope of success? Now, the international Qin Shi Huang, who possesses the navy, air force, and army, is flexing his muscles, knowing that the old methods of cutting wood and raising poles cannot defeat him, and so he prides himself on his power.

Aping 202

— Yongzi

Miss Xi Shi was a famous beauty in Chinese history. It is said that Miss Xi Shi's beauty lay in her having a heart condition, which caused her eyebrows to furrow. At that time, there happened to be a Miss Dong Shi, who did not have a heart condition but, in a flight of fancy, also held her heart with both hands and furrowed her brows, trying to compete with Miss Xi Shi to see who was prettier. However, Miss Xi Shi's holding her heart was like our East Asian weaklings, naturally ill, while Miss Dong Shi's holding her heart was artificial, making people sick to their stomachs. So there is a classic story called "Dong Shi Imitates Xi Shi," which mocks people for "drawing a tiger but ending up with a dog."

With the eastward spread of Western culture, Western misses and missies have begun to expand into China. Western misses and missies all wear high heels on their six-inch bound feet, and when they walk, their breasts shake in front and their buttocks sway in the back, which is indeed beautiful. Eastern misses and missies, seeing this, are envious and also put on high heels on their newly liberated feet, hobbling and twisting. As a result, they fall over, sprain their ankles, and perform countless other tricks. Western misses and missies are born with curly hair and long eyelashes. Eastern misses and missies feel that this is particularly charming, so they also perm their black hair and blacken their eyes, trying to compete to see who is prettier. Unfortunately, without bleaching their yellow skin and dyeing their black eyes and hair, no matter how closely they imitate, they cannot hide their true Dong Shi face.

Western misses and missies all talk about "socializing publicly," "free love," "female independence," and "gender equality." However, Eastern misses and missies, when imitating this, have achieved the cause of "different paths leading to the same goal," but the result of "different women" is that everything has become "romantic" and "indulgent," like wild horses without reins.

Xi Shi holding her heart and Dong Shi imitating her has become a joke for the ages. Are Eastern misses and missies imitating Western misses and missies in everything in a way that is just right? Please tell me if the imitators have succeeded.

East and West of Fourth Avenue 203

— Zhongqin

Every time I walk along this bustling Fourth Avenue, I always say to myself, "Friend, this is the road that leads you to enlightenment, that satisfies your desire for knowledge, and at the same time, it can also tempt you, squandering your youth and leading you to depravity! On the same road, there are two different paths, and you should pay attention to what lies ahead! Over there, infinite treasures await you, but over there, there are also animals more venomous than snakes and fiercer than beasts attracting you!" Especially at night, when I walk along Fourth Avenue, I repeat these words to myself, walking from east to west. Starting from Henan Road, there are many precious keys hanging there, waiting for their masters to take them, keys to open the doors of knowledge. The Commercial Press, China Bookstore, World Bookstore, Datong, Kaiming, Modern Publishing House, etc., are where these precious keys reside. You can go and take them. Young people should often seek the keys they need.

Further west, on the cement sidewalks in front of the World Bookstore, or on the sidewalks in front of the Qingguang Bookstore, when young pedestrians pass by, especially young people who look like students, there stands someone wearing a tattered long gown, holding a cigarette butt in his hand, and he hums beside the young people, "Want to buy *spring* [pornography]?" This is the first step in leading young people down the path of depravity.

Further west, all the way to Xizang Road, this section in the middle is the main camp for leading young people astray. Once the silver lights come on, a group of creatures adorned with small electric lights shuttle back and forth, beginning their deadly work. Young people are occasionally bewildered, drawn to the allure of beauty and pleasure, and the only result is to lose their footing and fall into depravity. However, many modern university students, and even middle school students, are unknowingly indulging in it, not realizing their peril until it's too late.

In short, Fourth Avenue is the central point of cultural undertakings, and also the main factory for manufacturing sin. On the same road, one east and one west, they show absolute opposites.

Fuzhou Under the Gaze of Hawks and Owls 204

— Hongqing

Because the enemy's fierce offensive has brazenly broken into the pass, with rumors spreading that its aim is not only Tianjin and Hebei, but also Shandong and Fujian, I can't help but think of Fuzhou. Fuzhou, separated from Taiwan by only a narrow stretch of water, has long been under the gaze of hawks and owls since Taiwan was ceded. Therefore, the Japanese expatriates in Fuzhou all carry a certain air of aggression, even though they are all doing business. The largest concentration of Japanese expatriates is in Nantai Fan Chuanpu, and the largest business is Osaka Shosen Kaisha, which domestic shipping companies cannot match. For example, when a domestic ship docks at Luoxing Pagoda in Mawei, the ships traveling to Fuzhou cannot directly reach the inland river. Small boats are used to transport passengers and goods to Nantai, charging an additional five jiao per person. Japanese ships do not charge extra, so naturally passengers prefer to travel on Japanese ships. Japanese expatriates also run a newspaper called "Min Bao," which serves as a mouthpiece for public opinion. Initially, it was written in Chinese, but later it was changed to a Chinese-Japanese bilingual format. This newspaper has a strong influence in Fuzhou, speaking frankly and without restraint, which naturally makes it popular among readers, surpassing the newspapers run by the Chinese themselves. In addition, there are also the Bo'ai Hospital and the Lushanxuan Photo Studio, both of which are very famous. There are also many prostitutes.

It is easy to see that the Japanese expatriates in Fuzhou have an air of aggression, unlike the expatriates from other countries who are mainly engaged in business. They have created a cherry blossom atmosphere in their residential area, and walking through it makes one feel as if they are no longer in Fuzhou, which is even more frightening! In particular, there are also many Taiwanese people who have forgotten their homeland and act as accomplices for the enemy, often engaging in acts of humiliation against the Chinese people. During Fang Shengtāo's administration, he handled matters properly, hoping that the province would be safe, but in the end, things still happened. Now that the enemy's fierce offensive has already broken into the pass, and Shandong and Fujian are within their ambitious grasp, when the time comes, the Japanese expatriates in the Nantai Fan Chuanpu area will undoubtedly be the vanguard. It all depends on how the current authorities prepare.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 205

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Brewing Tea to Pass the Long Night, Holding Guns Thinking of the Year's End, Raising High the Banner of Resistance Against Tyranny, Shouting Loudly

Gui Zhi smiled, "I'm not leaving, I'm pouring tea." Zhao Weng said with a smile, "That's good, let's not be strangers, we should be like family." As he spoke, he stroked his beard and nodded. Gui Zhi poured three cups of hot tea, and everyone shared them. Zhao Weng put down his cup, listened intently for a while, and said absentmindedly, "Am I drunk?" Yang Old Woman. Jiang Shi said with a smile, "You're not drunk." Zhao Weng hesitated and said, "Am I not drunk? If you say I'm not drunk, then this is really something new. How come tonight, on New Year's Eve, I can't hear a single firecracker?" Gui Zhi said, "Have you forgotten? There's martial law this year, and firecrackers are not allowed on New Year's Eve." Zhao Weng then stroked his beard, shook his head, and said, "I've lived in Beijing for fifty years, and this is the first time that firecrackers are not allowed on New Year's Eve." Gui Zhi pouted and said, "It's all because of those damn Japanese, they're causing trouble, so the government won't allow us to set off firecrackers." Zhao Weng shook his head and said, "This isn't the fault of the Japanese, it's because you Chinese people don't stand up for yourselves. I see on the map that Japan is ten times smaller than China. According to Ziqiang [son], Japan's population is only one-fifth of ours. Why are we letting them bully us? My Ziqiang is stupid. When he comes back, he always talks to me about the current situation, saying that he wants to be a commander and this and that. I tell him that a company commander should just fulfill his responsibilities as a company commander, and not talk about the things a commander does. Old woman, I'm different from other old men. I don't want my son to be a division or brigade commander, and I don't want to make millions or tens of thousands of silver dollars. Think about it, I'm so old, I'm almost in the grave, what use do I have for wealth and glory? But I just have this one son, and my son is a soldier. In a country on the verge of collapse like this, the fate of a soldier is really uncertain. I just have one selfish wish, to hold a grandson soon. If he can carry on the Zhao family line, I can die in peace." As he spoke, he poured himself another cup of tea and sat down to drink it. Jiang Shi said with a smile, "Isn't that an easy thing to do? You should find a young lady for the company commander as soon as possible." Zhao Weng took a sip of tea and sighed. "You don't know, my son has two friends with new ideas, and he reads newspapers and magazines himself. He says that the saying 'There are three unfilial acts, the greatest of which is to have no descendants' is not valid. As long as he is filial to his father, that's enough. It doesn't matter if he has a son or not." (May Fourth Movement)

Rambling Talk

The Customer Is Always Right 206

— Yin Feng

I have a friend who is most afraid of going to stores to buy things in his life, and he always entrusts others to do it if he can avoid going himself. Once I asked him why he was afraid of going to stores to buy things, was it because he was afraid of trouble? Was it because he wanted to save effort? But he sighed and said, "Neither, neither! I don't want to see the (unpleasant faces) and indifferent attitudes of these shop assistants, so I'm afraid of going to stores to buy things." Indeed, the faces and attitudes of many shop assistants can easily drive away customers and offend them, no wonder my friend looks at them with dread and dares not ask them anything, dismissing them entirely. No wonder people who come back from Europe, America, and Japan often praise the shop assistants in Europe, America, and Japan, how polite, humble, courteous, and patient they are to customers, and how they know how to do business. Recently, I saw a very valuable article in an American magazine, which is worth reading for Chinese businessmen. Now I will translate the gist of it as follows:

The dining cars of a certain railway in the northern United States are all contracted by a certain boss, and the business is very prosperous, and every customer is satisfied. According to general passengers, their satisfaction is not in the exquisiteness and deliciousness of the dishes, but in the thoughtfulness of the waiters' service.

In the past, a certain boss only opened a small tavern at the station. In this tavern, in addition to all the necessary equipment and decorations, there was also a very eye-catching slogan pasted on it, which read: "The customer is always right."

The boss on the one hand tried to improve the dishes, and on the other hand, he devoted all his efforts to training the waiters. The training method was very ingenious. Every day, he took one or two hours of free time to teach the waiters to be customers, and the old man acted as the waiter. How to greet, how to serve dishes, how to talk, how to collect money, how to see off guests, he personally taught them one by one.

The waiters here, in addition to keeping the sentence on the slogan in mind at all times, had to implement it anytime and anywhere. If a customer thought that a certain dish was not well done (in fact, it was very good, but he said it was not well done), he must change it. If the waiter did not allow it, then the boss, knowing it, would immediately (fire) the disobedient waiter without any room for negotiation, because the contract signed when entering the store already had a penalty clause of (immediate dismissal for offending customers).

Because a certain boss always adhered to the slogan "The customer is always right", he can always get the effect of "business is always good". If the friend I mentioned above saw this article, he would definitely sigh again and say: "Some stores in our country inconspicuously paste the slogan "The customer is always wrong", so they will always get the retribution of "business is always bad".

Advertising in Soviet Russia 207

— Xin Fo

In imperialist countries, commercial advertising is included in university courses, how sacred and solemn, businessmen intrigue and fight, and there are hundreds of techniques, which are promoted and expanded to what extent. But in Soviet Russia, where communism has been transformed from an ideal to a reality, and in our country, which has restored diplomatic relations after moving from an ideal to a reality, advertising has become a thing of the past, simply unnecessary. Because as long as the policy of public ownership of products exists, advertising will become a waste.

The most widely circulated newspaper in Soviet Russia now is called Pārvda (meaning Trust), with a daily circulation of two million copies, and of course it is a government organ. The so-called advertisements are only like the classified advertisements in Shen Bao, such as house rentals, job recruitment, furniture sales, and statements of loss. In addition, there are government announcements to the public on how to avoid tuberculosis, as well as warnings about drinking, how it makes people poor. There is nothing of a commercial advertising nature to speak of.

Then again, Soviet Russia is not unaware of the true meaning of commercial advertising. For all of their export industries, grains, seafood, etc., they pay great attention to the cleanliness and tidiness of packaging, the beauty of decoration and printing, and the novelty and uniqueness of the explanatory phrases, all of which are very much in line with the principles of advertising and possess the conditions of advertising. This spirit of selflessness is truly a great expression of national character.

Jiang Mengling's Talk 214

Li Dazhao was an old professor at Peking University. Out of friendship and affection, the school's president, Jiang Menglin, allowed fundraising to handle Li's funeral and burial. Unexpectedly, when the funeral took place, the students took actions outside the boundaries of the school. The reporter interviewed Jiang to inquire about the truth. He replied as follows: When Mr. Li Dazhao's coffin passed Xisi Pailou, suddenly more than a hundred students came and blocked the road to offer sacrifices, give speeches, and distribute leaflets. The military police stepped forward to stop them, so twenty students were arrested. I live in Maojiawan, which is close to Xisi Pailou. The car traveled to Xisi Beidajie, and I learned about this matter. So, I inquired with the military police about what happened, but I didn't get any results. I have now sent someone to inquire. The school authorities cannot interfere with students' actions outside the school. In recent years, the thinking of young students has leaned to the left, which is really dangerous. Spreading doctrine on the street is too stupid. Knowing that the military police are strict, why bother to throw yourself into the net? When Mr. Li's coffin passed Xizhimen, only Mrs. Li and her children and relatives were sending the coffin, and there were no students. By the time it was buried at the Wanan Cemetery in Xiangshan, it was already sunset. Mr. Li was lonely after his death, and his children were still young and studying in middle school, unable to support themselves. Because Mr. Li was an old professor at Peking University, his owed salary has already been paid in full, and a pension of 40 yuan per month will be issued for 20 months. The family's living expenses now depend on this. As for the cost of handling the funeral, it was raised by friends, totaling more than 600 yuan, and more than 300 yuan was used for the funeral. Because Li's coffin was parked in Miaoguangge, the parking fee had not been paid for many years. According to the person serving the spirit, more than 100 yuan in parking fees are owed, and they are currently discussing with the Zhejiang Tongxiang Association.

Executive Yuan Meeting Resolves that the Ministry of Education Will Compile Textbooks for Primary and Secondary Schools 215

The first phase of preliminary work can be completed by the end of this year

The Ministry of Education has announced the curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools, and all kinds of textbooks should be compiled in accordance with these standards to set an example. It is heard that the Ministry of Education plans to carry out this compilation work in three phases. The first phase of compilation is the textbooks that are most needed by primary and secondary schools at present, such as Chinese, arithmetic, civics, history, geography, and nature. The Ministry of Education will formulate a detailed plan, prepare a budget, and submit it to the Executive Yuan for discussion. The Executive Yuan meeting on the 25th has already discussed and passed it, and it can be started immediately. It is expected that the first phase of preliminary work can be completed by the end of this year. Starting in 1934, it can be promulgated throughout the country.

Local News

Shanghai Education Association Held First Secondary Education Research Conference Yesterday 216

▲ Appointed committee members to study in four groups

▲ Conveners drafted research outlines

The Shanghai Education Association held its first Secondary Education Research Committee meeting yesterday (26th) at 1:00 p.m. in the auditorium of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society. More than ten people attended, including Zhang Shilin, Qi Zhengcheng, Jin Xizhang, Xu Zeyi, Jin Yuezhang, Dai Yuheng, Sun Xiangzhong, and Chen Jicheng. Xu Zeyi chaired the meeting, and Chen Bangyan took the minutes. The meeting was opened as scheduled, and the chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting, and then the discussion began: (1) How should this association be divided into groups for research? (Resolved) Divide into (A) School Administration Group, (B) Subject Teaching Group, (C) National Defense Knowledge Group, and (D) Student Life Group. Each member of the association must at least identify with one group. (2) How should the research problem items for each group be specified? (Resolved) (A) The research problem items for the School Administration Group are: 1. School building problems, 2. Equipment problems, 3. Service and treatment problems for faculty and staff, 4. Student transfer problems, and 5. Integration of teaching and discipline problems. (B) The research problem items for the Subject Teaching Group are: Research by subject according to the newly promulgated curriculum standards. (C) The research problem items for the National Defense Knowledge Group are: 1. Issues related to Boy Scout training, 2. Issues related to military training, 3. Issues related to military sanitation, and 4. Issues related to air defense. (D) The research problem items for the Student Life Group are: 1. The mentor system problem, 2. The problem of stipulating moral education standards, 3. The method of examining conduct scores, 4. Reward and punishment problems, and 5. Student selection and career selection problems. (3) Appointed conveners for the first meeting of each group (Resolved) Dai Yuheng was appointed for the School Administration Group, Sun Xiangzhong was appointed for the Subject Teaching Group, Lu Hua was appointed for the National Defense Knowledge Group, and Zhang Shilin was appointed for the Student Life Group. (4) The conveners of the first meeting of each group should first draft research outlines for their respective groups, and ask the members of each group to submit proposals to the convener for sorting before the meeting. Can it be implemented? Please review the case. (Resolved) Passed. (5) Each group must hold at least one meeting in May (Resolved) Passed. (6) The secondary school graduation joint examination is about to be held. Should this association organize a (Secondary School Graduation Joint Examination Research Committee) to study the implementation methods of the graduation joint examination and submit them to the educational administrative organs for adoption and implementation? (Resolved) Dai Yuheng, Jin Yuezhang, Xu Zeyi, and other thirteen people were appointed as members. The first meeting was held immediately after the adjournment of the association. (7) What is the most suitable time for future meetings of this association? (Resolved) Changed to Sunday morning. (8) Appointed the chairman and vice chairman of this association (Resolved) After the number of members of this association is determined, they will be elected at the next meeting. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Vocational Education Society Holds Council Meeting 217

▲ It was decided that this year's annual meeting will be held in Kaifeng

▲ Next year, agricultural vocational schools and other undertakings will be established

The Chinese Vocational Education Society held a council meeting at Yizhi Xiang Restaurant on Fourth Avenue at 6:00 p.m. yesterday (25th). Cai Yuanpei, Gao Jian, Ou Yuanhuai, Liao Maoru, Jia Foru, Pan Xulun, Gu Yinting, Chen Binhe, Liu Zhanen, Wang Zhixin, Du Chongyuan, Zhu Jingnong, and Zou Bingwen attended. Cai Yuanpei chaired the meeting and performed the ceremony as usual. First, the chairman gave an opening speech, followed by a report on the matters: (1) Yang Weiyu reported on the status of the headquarters of this society and the research, promotion, and editing departments, as well as the recent economic situation. (2) Jia Foru reported on the status of industry and commerce education. (3) Yao Huiquan reported on the status of remedial education and rural improvement. (4) Pan Yangyao reported on the status of vocational guidance. Then, the discussion began: (1) The Henan Provincial Department of Education invited this year's annual meeting to be held in Kaifeng, please vote on the case. Resolved, it was decided to hold it in Kaifeng. The date is tentatively scheduled for late July, and a notice will be issued after obtaining the consent of Bianfang [Kaifeng]. (2) Should this year's annual meeting submit important issues for discussion? Resolved, the following five cases were submitted: (A) Use the original equipment of schools to promote vocational remedial education. (B) Promote rural sideline training. (C) Train vocational education teachers. (D) Hold a mobile lecture on production education. (E) Ordinary middle schools should establish experimental factories or farms. (3) Please recommend members of the staff qualification review committee. Resolved, Pan Xulun, Ou Yuanhuai, and Liao Maoru were recommended as reviewers. (4) Should this society add new undertakings next year? Resolved, it is proposed to handle the following four items and hand them over to the office department to provide detailed plans: (A) Agricultural vocational school, (B) Unemployment insurance, (C) Sales office, (D) Industrial remedial education.

Sports

Second Annual Citywide Inter-School Joint Sports Meeting Opens 218

The opening ceremony will be held at the China Athletics Field starting at 1:00 p.m.

More than 4,000 male and female athletes from 66 participating schools

The second annual citywide inter-secondary school joint sports meeting, hosted by the Municipal Bureau of Education, opened at the China Athletics Field on Father Laroque Road at 1:00 p.m. today. It will last for three days. There are sixty-six participating male and female schools, and more than 1,000 male and female athletes. More than 2,000 people participated in the general exercises, and there should be more than 4,000 athletes participating in the group performances. It will be an unprecedented grand occasion. After a long period of rain, the weather is now clear, with a gentle breeze and a bright sun. The athletes will be even more energetic to win the championship.

Venue Layout

丨 Wireless radio broadcasting of news 219

The venue is the China Athletics Field on Father Laroque Road. The entrance for visitors is at the Malong Road intersection. There is a tall tower archway at the entrance, which is very majestic. The rostrum is on the west side of the running circle in the venue. The stage is full of prizes donated by various sectors of society. A couplet is hung in front of the stage, which reads: (Hope young people exercise their bodies and become models for athletes; wish many scholars to improve physical education and show the spirit of our nation.) A military band stage is set up on the right side of the stage. The Municipal Public Security Bureau Band is invited to play music during the opening ceremony. A rescue station is set up on the left side of the stage. The Municipal Health Bureau is invited to send personnel to take care of all security matters in the venue. The male athletes' rest area is on the east side of the running circle, and the female athletes' rest area is on the north side of the running circle. A wireless radio broadcaster is set up in the venue to broadcast all news.

▲Instruction from the Municipal Education Bureau Regarding Nanyang Commercial High School: The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued the following instruction yesterday to Wu Xinglian, principal of the Private Nanyang Commercial Senior High School: "Upon investigation, this school has been repeatedly accused of enticing athletes Fu Jincheng and Zeng Rongzhong from the Private Jiangnan Institute of Physical Education in early April of this year, preparing them to participate in the Municipal Secondary School Joint Sports Meeting in order to win prizes, etc. This Bureau dispatched personnel to investigate, and it was reported that Fu and Zeng were indeed enrolled in the school on April 7th. The enrollment of Fu and Zeng in the school exceeded the prescribed enrollment period. This school should cancel the academic registration of the two students and instruct them to return to the Private Jiangnan Institute of Physical Education for studies. As for the school's mid-term enticement of students to participate in this year's Secondary School Joint Sports Meeting, it has been resolved at the 261st Bureau Affairs Meeting of this Bureau to issue a reprimand to the school principal and the physical education teacher, and to suspend the school's participation in this year's Secondary School Joint Sports Meeting track and field events. This order is hereby issued for your respective information and compliance."

Next Year's Far Eastern Games Scheduled

May 12-19 in Manila, Philippines Sends Notification and Invitation to Participate 225

The 10th Far Eastern Games, according to the schedule, will be held in the Philippines next year. The Philippine Sports Association has decided to hold them in Manila from May 12th to 19th next year (1934). The China National Sports Federation has received its official notification and invitation, inviting China to send athletes to participate at that time.

Participation Notice 226

丨Each School Provides its Own Performance Equipment丨

1. Athletes' bibs should be sewn on the front and back of their sports uniforms with thread. 2. For any discrepancies or omissions in the assignment of events, please correct them before the start of the event. 3. If the events registered by the athletes of each school exceed the regulations, the last event registered by the athlete will be removed. 4. Relay races are not divided into groups. Male students can register for the 800-meter and 1600-meter events, and female students can register for the 400-meter event. Each school selects four athletes to compete. 5. The numbers of the athletes in the ball game performances will be provided by each school. 6. For the group gymnastics performance, each school should provide a white card (one for each type) with the school name, performance name, and the name of the physical education teacher. Hand it over to the group gymnastics judge when entering the field. 7. The equipment used in the calisthenics should be moved to the field and installed by each school before the performance. 8. Each school shall provide the equipment used in the national martial arts. 9. The conference program will follow the schedule for various competitions. Any changes will be announced by the chief referee to the announcer for temporary reporting. 10. The standing positions of the students participating in the gymnastics will be designated by the conference, and a diagram will be provided for clarification. Please follow the diagram, single file column, to align with the command platform, each row occupying about 50 people.

Important Notice 227

▲Teachers and Staff of Each School are Not Allowed to Enter the Sports Circle

(1) Physical education teachers and other faculty members of each school are not allowed to enter the sports circle. (2) The bibs of track and field athletes must be firmly attached on both the front and back, and should not be folded. Violators will not have their results recorded. (3) Track and field Group B athletes must have their weight and height measured each time after the preliminary and final rounds. (4) Students participating in the gymnastics should arrive at the field at 12:00 noon and line up according to the order specified in the arrangement diagram. A preliminary practice should be conducted before the opening ceremony.

Judging Rules 228

丨Attention to Those Who Raise Protests丨

Concise Rules of the Judging Committee for the 2nd Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Joint Sports Meeting: Article 1. This Committee shall be organized by five to seven members appointed by the President. Article 2. The powers of this Committee shall be to adjudicate and handle all protests concerning competition and sportsmanship. Article 3. The decisions of this Committee shall be final and no further protests shall be allowed. Article 4. The President shall appoint one of the members as the Chairman. Article 5. The meetings of this Committee shall not be held on a fixed date and shall be convened by the Chairman at any time. Article 6. The meeting of this Committee must have a quorum of more than half of the members to be convened. Article 7. These rules shall be implemented with the approval of the President.
