Discussions

Only Afraid That China Will Not Perish 288

— Wu

Since the Japanese army invaded Rehe, it seems that the whole country has been in a state of panic again. The telegrams such as "(requesting to fight against Japan)" and "(determined to resist)" are certainly busy, especially the officials and dignitaries who are fleeing east and west, even more busy and sweating profusely. Recently, Rehe has finally come to a complete end, which could have "(come to an end)," but the Japanese imperialists are still not satisfied. Judging from the fact that they asked for ancient books to be evacuated after the antiques and national treasures were moved out of Beiping, we know that Tianjin and Beijing are indeed in danger. Under the most effective "(consistent policy)," they are probably not very reliable, so the mouthpiece of imperialist hirelings, the literati and doctoral students, cannot but be sincerely fearful and busy, and even publicly publish so-called "(nothing more than that)" (opinions).

Regarding this doctoral student, we know him very clearly. "(In November of the year before last, he advocated that the government authorities should accept the five basic principles proposed by the Japanese government in the League of Nations and begin negotiations)," and "(in June of last year, he wrote an article advocating that the government should express its willingness to conduct negotiations with Japan based on the above five principles)," and now he has repeatedly stated: "(I firmly believe that no matter what method is adopted for negotiations with Japan, it must not violate the principles of the report and recommendations passed by the League of Nations at its General Assembly on February 24 this year)." This is said most clearly. In simple terms, it means that there is no other way except to sincerely and willingly "(directly negotiate)" with Japanese imperialism. Moreover, it is absolutely not allowed to "(fight desperately at the risk of death)," so he said "(I cannot go against my conscience and advocate war)."

Of course, this kind of "(opinion)" is very commendable under the current situation of "(strategic)" followed by "(luring the enemy in)," followed by "(defending)," followed by "(preparing to counterattack)," and if it really pleases the enlightened monarch, he will inevitably be appointed as a high-ranking official. The emperor is talented and saves the world, turns clouds into rain, and the sea is calm, and the world celebrates together.

However, the most regrettable thing is that "(expanding the national revolutionary war)" has become the most powerful argument in the country. The broad masses of people have recognized that only revolutionary war is the only way out for the Chinese nation, and only his group of high-level Chinese people will be so humble and lick the master's spittle with a wagging tail. Naturally, those heroes who swear to resist to the death will not dare to immediately cover up their flags and cease their drums. At least in the newspapers, they still have to solemnly "(deal with the enemy)." Therefore, people cannot but cover their noses and dare not smell this public opinion.

So, why does he make such a big fuss? In a word, he is only afraid that China will not perish.

Alas! Is this what is called "(when a country is about to perish, there must be monsters)?"

○ ○ ○ ○ ○ ○ □ ○ ○

Laundress 289

— Wen

｜Cannot Wash Away the Stains of the World｜

In the north of Shanghai, a small room at the end of an alley, full of garbage and the stinging stench of urine, is where the laundress struggles hard to make a living.

Every morning, the distant, wailing sound of the factory whistle is her accurate timepiece and the signal to start work. She pulls out a large lead bucket of clothes soaked in soapy water from the corner of the door, puts it close to the tap, and turns around to button her clothes. With both hands grabbing her bushy, sparrow's nest-like gray hair, she lifts another lead bucket and treads the desolate morning light to the tiger stove at the entrance of the alley to make hot water. In the old days, she couldn't even bear to part with the few coins for hot water. She only needed to soak the clothes in cold water from time to time, then lightly rub some soap on them, and brush them hard with a clothes brush, and they would be clean. But now she no longer has the strength, so she can only use hot water.

When the sun rises and there are cries of vegetable vendors at the entrance of the alley, and the manure cart is rumbling on the stone-paved road, she carries two buckets of clothes of uneven texture, walking and resting, to the open space on the right outside the alley to hang them out to dry. Once they are hung up, her head spins, and the houses around her seem to be spinning. So she wipes her forehead with her right hand, slowly sits on a piece of wood, takes two deep breaths, and then has the strength to look up at the sky to see if there are any rain-like clouds. Every time it rains, she is always in a fluster and doesn't have time to tidy up, causing her to stumble and fall. Sometimes she brings rags to patch, but since she broke her old glasses in a sudden rain one day, she has had to stop this incidental work of patching.

In the afternoon, before evening, she takes the clothes back in and carefully folds them, sorting out the owners. Her face, wrinkled like chicken skin, always shows some hard-won smiles. She has finally completed a day's work, reducing a journey in life. She uses a yellowish-brown turban, neatly wrapped, and walks out of the door, out of the alley, to deliver them to the door. When people take them and look carefully, they shout at her, "(Not bad, washed fairly clean!)" She then replies with one sentence: "(Are there any more to wash? It would be good to take them along!)" Regardless of the quality of the material, she takes seven coins for each piece of clothing and pants, and three coins for each piece of socks, pillowcases, and vests. As long as she doesn't calculate incorrectly, she never argues. Her eyes shine with the light of contentment, and she reaches out with a slight tremor to receive the money. When the money reaches her hand, she says, "(Thank you!)"

Page 18

During the winter season, the weather is suddenly cold, and everyone is a little shivering, so the clothes are changed less frequently, but she still expects to work the same way, only her neck is a little shrunk. When she goes door to door to collect clothes,

When asked, or someone asks her why she is so unafraid of the cold and so able to endure hardship, she can be heard answering: "(The famine in my hometown drove me here? People say this place is paradise, but I still have to go hungry. When it comes to this time (winter), there is really only the north wind to drink! My husband pulls a rickshaw, but it can only feed his own mouth. Really, the poor only have the north wind to drink! Alas!)"

In fact, it is indeed somewhat like that. When winter comes, everyone is a little shivering, and clothes are changed less frequently, as if there is such a meaning:

Ah, poor laundress, you can only wash away the stains of the world?)

The Birth of the Silent Gourd 290

— Han

"(Mystery)" is a title given to the Chinese by Westerners. Probably they think that the Chinese national character and the things that Chinese people do are mostly different from theirs, or beyond reason and common sense, so their observations of the Chinese are also inexplicable, and this title of "(mystery)" has become good material for Westerners to laugh at.

Indeed, Chinese affairs are somewhat elusive. For example: it was originally spiritual unity to jointly face national disasters, but we ourselves put on a full martial arts performance. On the front line, blood and flesh fly everywhere, but in the rear, we have dancing to save the country. Today we send telegrams to kill the enemy, but tomorrow we quietly slip away. The more loudly we speak, the more tricks there are, and the more bizarre and colorful it is, so much so that we ourselves cannot help but feel comical. Even Westerners, when they see it, may shout: "This child is the most slippery of them all, my eyes are blurred!"

However, the Japanese are smart after all, and they guessed that the secret to solving the mystery is artillery, so the "(mystery)" that has been misunderstood for a long time.

Cheap Price, the Buyers Are Always Thinking Like This 291

The veil on his face was torn off with a loud bang on "(September 18th)," and oh! "(Mystery)" turned out to be just that.

However, the Chinese are ultimately difficult to understand. The old mystery has already been exposed, but a new silent gourd has been born. At present, the deep meaning of this silent gourd is profound and far-reaching, and the little ones are ignorant and dare not speculate rashly, but the Westerners may only know one or two, and the mystery of the matter lies in what medicine is hidden, and outsiders should not easily peek into the secret. However, according to routine calculations, there may not be another brilliant trick, and when the signboard is uncovered, I am afraid it is just a dark mass.

Recently, the mysterious gourd seems to be faintly releasing some faint sounds, as if saying: "It is difficult for eastern Hebei to fall, which does not hinder the overall situation, and besides, victory or defeat is a common thing for military strategists. Accepting adversity calmly, it is better to hold on to tranquility. Although it has not been welcomed by the enemy, the style of yielding and giving way by the elders has long been promoted throughout the world."

Then, it further warned: "When the Di people invaded Bin, King Tai moved to Qi. Being strong but not resisting is an ancient teaching. They use strength, we use gentleness; they use movement, we use stillness; sit and wait for ten years, the three islands will have earthquakes, and there will be a revolution in Tokyo. When luck comes, who will the final victory belong to but us!"

The author heard this and couldn't help but jump for joy three hundred times and shout wildly, "Long live the birth of the new silent gourd!"

Clerk Correspondence

A Matter of Life and Death 292

Editor Sir;

Every time I see you explain the doubts of the clerks in your newspaper, I can't help but feel the depression that has accumulated in my heart for several months surge to my head; so I venture to ask for your guidance:

I am a small employee in a company in this port, and my monthly income is still considerable. Five years ago (at the age of sixteen), with the idea of ​​my family and with my own consent, I got engaged to Miss Chen. Chen has also met me several times; both sides' temperament and family circumstances are quite suitable. Unexpectedly, in the year of the engagement, because I was bullied by my stepmother at home and was too busy at school, I developed scrofula. I am now twenty-one years old, and in these five years of living with the disease, although I have been treated by doctors in various ports, it has not been effective after all. Last spring, because of her age, the other party repeatedly asked to get married. For the sake of my remaining body, I declined several times. This spring, I felt comforted by all parties, so I made a firm decision and went to a certain hospital on Baker Road in this port for surgery. Although I have undergone two operations, according to the doctor's diagnosis, it is difficult to recover in a short time, and I definitely need to rest and recuperate. For the sake of my health, of course, I cannot get married in the near future; but if the other party continues to ask, then what method can I use to satisfy the other party? It really makes it difficult for me to the utmost. With twelve thousand points of sincerity, I hope that you can give me a satisfactory solution in a short period of time, that would be truly grateful. Sincerely wish you

Health, Gu Yousan respectfully 293

X X X X

Editor's note: Gu Jun's illness, as the doctor has determined, is difficult to recover in a short time, so it is of course advisable not to get married. Because the result of marriage is not only extremely dangerous for your health, but also harmful and unprofitable for Miss Chen. You feel that when they come to ask for marriage, there is no way to refuse; this is entirely because your concept is wrong. You only know that not getting married is "(for the sake of protecting health)," so you feel that it is inevitable to be selfish and inconvenient to speak. You should know that the reason for not getting married is mostly for the sake of taking care of the other party, then you will be justified. If they really insist on meeting and must get married, you only have the method of rather terminating the engagement. A matter of life and death does not allow submission.

Novel

Fleeting Moments in a Dream (Continuation Thirty-Eight) 294

— Qin Shouou

Inside, there were about sixteen or seventeen tables. As usual, the tables were piled with writing brushes, ink, paper, and the like, but there wasn't a single person in sight. All the people were crowded tightly together in one corner like ants. Several were laughing and gesticulating, several were counting money, and several were discussing with avid interest. Everyone was focused intently on something in the middle. No one noticed that Wu Yi had arrived from behind. Wu Yi also didn't want to disturb them, so with his hands behind his back, he quietly walked over and mingled into their group.

In the middle of the crowd was an ordinary office table, but there were no writing materials on the table. There was only a piece of white paper spread out, and on the paper, the Arabic numerals one, two, three, and four were written in large red ink, as well as the numbers (one three) and (two four), each a bit smaller. On each of these numbers, there was a considerable amount of money – coins, silver dollars, and banknotes were all present. At the head of the table sat a clerk with a serious demeanor. In front of him, besides a large pile of banknotes and silver, there was also an overturned porcelain jar. This person's hands were firmly pressed on the jar.

"Is everything ready?"

"Ready! Open!" The people around simultaneously urged him with a sense of fatalism. The person then let go of his hands and lifted the overturned porcelain jar. This reveal was no small matter. It immediately made everyone around shrink three inches. Each person bent over, eagerly stretching out their necks to look at what was on the table. Wu Yi also busily squeezed into a gap and peered intently.

What was under the jar turned out to be a pile of enamel badges, about the size of two dimes, of the "(National Universities Professors' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association)." There were approximately twenty or thirty of them. The person sitting in the center then divided them into groups of four, distributing them one group at a time. After the division, of course, there was a remainder.

"One! Haha! Picking the heavy with the light!" This time, the remainder was one. So the person in the center grabbed a lot of money and laughed contentedly. Many of the kind folks who had placed money on the numbers (two), (three), or (four) hung their heads dejectedly, muttering all sorts of vulgar curses.

"Haha! Old Huang! Three dollars in the bag!" One fellow, who had probably bet on the number (one) and profited from it, was so excited that he forgot himself for a moment. Turning around, without looking carefully, he reached out and grabbed Wu Yi's shoulder, shaking him vigorously and laughing.

"Friend! Excuse me! May I say a few words?" Wu Yi raised his voice and said these three sentences, immediately waking up the group of National Salvation Association staff members who were wildly gambling. The gentleman who had grabbed him, needless to say, had long since let go. Wu Yi's face, however, was without any sign of anger, just smiling. "My name is Wu Yi. I happen to be one of the executive committee members of this association! But I've never been here before. I didn't know that you all often relax here. Now that I know, I can't do anything about it. However, I have one request. I hope you will convey it to Executive Committee Member Doctor Li. Please ask him, for my sake, to take down that horizontal plaque above the door starting today!"

Wu Yi's sudden appearance and his sharp, cold words truly made this group of reveling gentlemen feel quite uneasy. No one knew how to deal with it.

"Goodbye! I wish you happiness!" The old doctor, filled with disappointment, walked away with small steps.

Film Special

Interesting Anecdotes from the London Screening of "Moonlight Serenade on the Spring River" 295

— Xin Fu

One Hundred Prospective Brides Attend the Theater

On the evening of the London screening of "Tell Me Tonight," jointly produced by Gaumont and British International Pictures, one hundred prospective brides suddenly arrived one after another. Their prospective grooms were none other than Jan Kiepura, the male lead in the film, who is a very famous Polish singer. As it turned out, Jan Kiepura was held up by other matters and could not attend, so a new date was set. How did this mysterious event come about? Listen to the explanation next time.

It started when Jan Kiepura was filming this movie. A reporter went to the studio to interview him. He inadvertently let slip that he would very much like to find an English woman to marry. Unexpectedly, the reporter published his words in the newspaper. Imagine, with his reputation and charm, plus an annual income of thirty-five thousand pounds, how could he not be admired and envied by European girls? As a result, letters of application flooded in, totaling more than seventeen thousand. Among them were English girls, Scottish ladies, and Irish misses; and most of the letters included beautiful photographs of the applicants. Jan Kiepura was now richer than if he had opened a large photography studio.

Later, when the film was finished, and ready for a screening at a theater in London. Jan Kiepura happened to be performing elsewhere, but he still carried the seventeen thousand letters with him. He selected one hundred letters from the many. He copied the names and addresses of these one hundred ladies and sent them to his London representative, telling him that he must invite these one hundred ladies to attend the screening of "Moonlight Serenade on the Spring River," and that he also planned to come to London to meet them after the film.

However, Jan Kiepura did not give the details of this matter in his letter, so at the time, neither the film company nor his representative could guess why he wanted to invite so many female guests. But since he had sent a letter, they had to follow his instructions in a confused state. On the day of the screening, all the invited female guests did arrive. Unexpectedly, Jan Kiepura did not have time to come, so these one hundred ladies, after the film, not being greeted by anyone, had to leave in disappointment. Later, Jan Kiepura told people the story, and everyone understood. But according to himself, this action was not entirely a joke. He really wanted to find an ideal bride among these one hundred ladies!

Film Review

A Review of "Dangerously Yours" 296

— Lei

The story is as follows: A well-dressed jewel thief steals jewelry from an old widow. At the time, only a young girl knows his secret, but because she loves the thief, she runs away with him. Later, although she strongly urges him to hand over the stolen goods, she is imprisoned by the thief. One day, she seizes an opportunity to escape into the sea. From then on, the thief, touched by the girl's virtue, has a change of heart, returns all the jewelry to its original owner, and eventually lives happily ever after with the girl.

A story like this is, of course, meaningless. But only American film professionals would be willing to spend so much money and energy on it. In this situation, we can see how far American cinema has fallen.

Speaking of the director, he naturally cannot create a great work from a mediocre script. But even so, in terms of the performance, he can't even clearly tell us the story. This must be said to be the director's immaturity. The entire film uniformly lacks a clear system, and it pays no attention to acting but focuses on unnecessary dialogue. However, the use of the camera is not so bad. Several exterior shots of the sea are also very good. Also, the way the girl's two cries for help on the boat are covered up in different ways is a clever point of the director and a highlight of the play. Like the scene of the spiritualist performing magic, is also very good.

As for the performances, they are extremely mediocre. The male lead is so lazy and unenthusiastic, and the female lead uses a middle-aged woman to play a young girl, which is unpleasant. There are no brilliant performances among the supporting roles. Only the unimportant female character who throws the cards has a bit of special charm. As for that clown, we seem to have seen him in "The Merry Widow", but his few expressions here, although not so stiff, cannot make people laugh. So the play's few "gags" are also ineffective.

Other aspects: The light’s spatial and temporal distinctions are very realistic. Especially the two scenes of the spiritualist performing magic, are very beautiful. The sets are mediocre and lack distinctive loopholes. The sound recording is pure enough to pass. But even with these achievements, it still can't bring the play up to standard, can it?

The Yueming Film Company is famous for producing martial arts films. Recently, it has changed its style. The image on the right is a scene from the company director Ren Pengnian’s new work "Blood Letter", starring Little Star Xiao Wulizhu, who is Ren’s beloved daughter. It is said that this film will be released at the Central Grand Theater soon.

The Famous Film "Desire" Premieres Tonight (Thursday) 297

— Niao

丨At the Paris Grand Theater丨

The latest production from the French Gaumont Film Company, "Desire"

Princess Tarakanova is an unprecedented historical masterpiece, depicting the licentiousness of the Russian Empress Catherine II during her reign, the greed of the Gypsy girl, and the aloofness of Princess Tarakanova, all of which are deeply moving. The female lead, Edith Jehanne, is most skilled in inner performance. In the play, she plays two characters with different personalities (namely, the Gypsy girl and Tarakanova), and both of them match the identities of the characters in the play. The costumes and sets throughout the film are rich and magnificent, and the harmony and melodiousness of the music are unique since European films began. It was created under the guidance of French master musicians, combining the strengths of Germany and Russia. Anyone with a special fondness for music will definitely feel its greatness. The film will premiere at the Paris Theater starting tonight at 9:30.

American Highway Film 298

— Si Ping

Recently screened at the American Club, with many Chinese and Westerners attending

The American Chamber of Commerce screened an American highway sound film at the Citibank Club on Monday evening. Leaders from Chinese and foreign political, business, and academic circles were invited to attend, making it a grand occasion. Before the highway film was screened, American Chamber of Commerce President Frank Hsu and American Commercial Counselor Arnold gave brief welcome and introduction speeches. The most essential sentence was that highway development occupies a very important position in modern Chinese transportation. The United States builds highways to facilitate transportation and also hopes to help other countries do such construction. After the speeches, the highway film was screened. The film showed us the completion of the American highway plan in 1930, with representatives from fifty-one countries being invited to visit. Representatives from various countries set off from Washington, D.C., traveling by long-distance bus, and were shown each section with subtitles explaining it. American highways total three million miles. Some are funded by the federal government, some are funded by state governments, and some are built by local governments. From the Canadian border in the north to the southernmost Mexican border, from the Atlantic coast in the east to the South Pacific coast, they run horizontally and vertically through states, cities, and villages. People with cars can drive wherever they want, going anywhere they please. Americans are so happy! The film shows us the progress from the slow manual road construction of the past to the rapid machine road construction of the present, as well as the construction of concrete hard-surfaced main roads and convenient branch roads, layer by layer. In some places, there is a railway above and a highway below, or a highway above and a railway below, intersecting in a cross shape. Finally, the film shows the highway network of each state in a statistical form, which is densely layered like a net. After watching it, one can't help but be envious and think that if the money that has been sent abroad to buy military supplies to fuel internal strife in China for more than twenty years could be used to build roads or build other public welfare projects, it would be quite impressive.

Movie Novel "Cavalcade" (9) 302

— Ne

Joe had gone through several wars and fortunately had not encountered any accidents. From 1914, 1915, until 1918, in these dark years, he still returned to London from time to time to find his lover, Fanny, and live their life of love. That day was an evening in 1918. Joe and Fanny had dinner together and returned to Fanny's dressing room. Joe was about to leave for the front again. They were reluctant to part. Fanny gave Joe a gold locket with a small portrait of herself inside, instructing him to keep it close to him. Joe instructed her to write to him every day. Outside the dressing room, music was playing. The curtain on the stage was rising and falling, one play after another. Fanny's dressing room door had been knocked several times, urging her to go out. At the last minute, Fanny was still reluctantly saying sweet words to Joe. Outside, they were shouting, "Miss Bridges, hurry up!" So she had to go out. At the moment of parting, Joe carefully looked at Fanny's face. Her smile, her courage, her tears, her inner pain, had all been deeply imprinted in his heart, until his death. But in another month or two, everything would be over!

On this day, Armistice Day in 1918, Keien's maid returned and said, "Mrs. Bridges is here to visit." Keien suspiciously invited her in. Ellen was very proud, wearing Parisian fashion, holding opera glasses in her hand, and was imperious, not at all like a servant to her former mistress. Keien reached out and said, "Ellen, I never dreamed it was you." Ellen did not shake her hand. She said, "I have a very important matter to discuss with you." Keien said, "That's great, I've been wanting to see you. Please sit down and tell me everything, how is Fanny?" Ellen said angrily: "I came for her, for her and Joe"! Keien asked in surprise, "Joe?" Ellen said: Yes. They:::I don't have to hide it, they already have a relationship. I think::: (What do you think)? Keien's happiness born from the armistice had all disappeared. Ellen said: "Now that the war has stopped, Joe will be back soon, I think they should get married." Keien asked Ellen if Fanny knew she was coming. Ellen shook her head. Keien felt relieved. Fortunately, Fanny was not that kind of gold digger, otherwise Joe would have a relationship with this kind of woman and would not know how to love herself. She said to Ellen: "This matter can only be discussed when Joe comes back. I never interfere in my son's affairs. You should have discussed it with Fanny before you came. This question can only be discussed later. Goodbye, Ellen."

Ellen heard this and had to slowly retreat towards the door of the guest room. But she suddenly turned around again and said to Keien in anger: "Don't think that Fanny is not worthy of marrying your son? If you think that way, you are wrong! Fanny is popular everywhere, and all the people she associates with are first-class figures. Moreover, it is not like before, everything has changed. However, some people move forward with the times, and some people are willing to fall behind." (To be continued)
